## Domain Knowledge (LLM-generated)
**Domain**: thermomechanical constitutive modeling (materials science)
**Analysis**: This task models the stress-strain-temperature relationship of a material. Stress depends on strain through elastic or plastic constitutive laws, while temperature modulates mechanical properties through thermal softening, modulus reduction, or thermally activated deformation mechanisms.

**Common formula structures in this domain**:
- Hooke's law (temperature-dependent): sigma = c0 * epsilon (linear elasticity at fixed T)
- Temperature-dependent elastic modulus: sigma = c0 * (c1 - c2 * T) * epsilon (linear modulus decrease with T)
- Power-law hardening: sigma = c0 * epsilon**c1 (Hollomon-type strain hardening)
- Power-law with thermal softening: sigma = c0 * epsilon**c1 * exp(c2 * T) (combined hardening and thermal effects)
- Ramberg-Osgood type: sigma = c0 * epsilon + c1 * epsilon**c2 (elastic-plastic transition)
- Johnson-Cook simplified: sigma = (c0 + c1 * epsilon**c2) * (c3 - c4 * T) (strain hardening with linear thermal softening)
- Johnson-Cook with homologous temperature: sigma = (c0 + c1 * epsilon**c2) * (c3 - c4 * T**c5) (power-law thermal softening)
- Arrhenius-type thermal activation: sigma = c0 * epsilon**c1 * exp(c2 * (c3 * T)) (thermally activated flow stress)
- Voce hardening with temperature: sigma = c0 * (c1 - exp(c2 * epsilon)) * exp(c3 * T) (saturating hardening with thermal softening)
- Ludwik model: sigma = c0 + c1 * epsilon**c2 (yield stress plus power-law hardening)
- Temperature-modulated Ludwik: sigma = (c0 + c1 * epsilon**c2) * exp(c3 * T) (Ludwik with Arrhenius thermal factor)
- Polynomial stress-strain: sigma = c0 * epsilon + c1 * epsilon**2 + c2 * epsilon**3 (nonlinear elastic/hyperelastic)
- Hyperbolic sine flow: sigma = c0 * T * asinh(c1 * epsilon * exp(c2 * (c3 * T))) (Garofalo/Sellars-Tegart creep model)
- Bilinear with temperature: sigma = c0 * epsilon * (c1 + c2 * T) + c3 * T (linear coupling between strain and temperature)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope → Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects → Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay → Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior → Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects → Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- Linear thermal softening → Multiplicative factor (1 - c*T) or (c0 - c1*T) applied to stress, reflecting modulus decrease with temperature
- Strain hardening saturation → Voce-type form (1 - exp(-c*epsilon)) indicating dislocation density saturation
- Power-law strain hardening → epsilon**c with 0 < c < 1 (typically c ≈ 0.1-0.5 for metals), reflecting work hardening
- Arrhenius thermal activation → exp(-c/T) or exp(c*T) factors representing thermally activated dislocation motion or diffusion
- Yield stress offset → Additive constant c0 in stress expression representing initial yield strength independent of strain
- Homologous temperature scaling → T raised to a power T**c in softening terms, capturing nonlinear thermal degradation
- Strain-temperature coupling → Product terms epsilon*T or epsilon**c1 * T**c2 representing interaction between mechanical and thermal effects
- Hyperbolic sine stress dependence → sinh(c*sigma) or asinh(c*epsilon) appearing in high-temperature creep regimes bridging power-law and exponential behavior

**GT:** `7.723*epsilon**3 + 36.659*epsilon**0.2144*exp(-82.437/(8.314*T)) + 1.336*epsilon*(T - 327.264)**2`

`epsilon*(T - 327.264)**2 = epsilon*(T² - 654.529*T + 107,102.0)`
`= epsilon*T² - 654.529*epsilon*T + 107,102.0*epsilon`

`7.723*epsilon**3 + 36.659*epsilon**0.2144*exp(-9.914/T) + 1.336*epsilon*T² - 874.452*epsilon*T + 143,088.3*epsilon`

This is crucial - the GT has `exp(-c/T)`, not `exp(c*T)`. Most candidates with exponentials use `exp(T*c)`, which cannot match `exp(-c/T)`.

The GT has these basis functions:
1. `epsilon**3` (polynomial)
2. `epsilon**0.2144 * exp(-9.916/T)` (fractional power times Arrhenius-type exponential)
3. `epsilon * T²` (cross term)
4. `epsilon * T` (cross term)
5. `epsilon` (linear)

Note: The exponential term is `exp(-c/T)`, NOT `exp(c*T)`. This is crucial.

Let me check each candidate for structural compatibility:

**Key structural requirements:**
- Must have `epsilon**3` or equivalent
- Must have `epsilon^(~0.21) * exp(-const/T)` — this is an Arrhenius form `exp(-c/T)`, not `exp(c*T)`
